<mi>P</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>work done per unit time</mtext>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<mi>Q</mi>
<mi>V</mi>
</mrow>
<mi>t</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>I</mi>
<mi>V</mi>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P={\text{work done per unit time}}={\frac {QV}{t}}=IV\,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="P = \text{work done per unit time} = \frac {QV}{t} = IV \," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/53a84ac821c54d1255c69e9a140f728a54fb8158" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:42.824ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where
</p>
<dl><dd><i>Q</i> is electric charge in <a href="/wiki/Coulomb" title="Coulomb">coulombs</a></dd>
<dd><i>t</i> is time in seconds</dd>
<dd><i>I</i> is electric current in <a href="/wiki/Ampere" title="Ampere">amperes</a></dd>
<dd><i>V</i> is electric potential or voltage in <a href="/wiki/Volt" title="Volt">volts</a></dd></dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">Electricity generation</a> is often done by a process of converting mechanical energy to electricity. Devices such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steam_turbines" title="Steam turbines">steam turbines</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_turbines" title="Gas turbines">gas turbines</a> are involved in the production of the mechanical energy, which is passed on to <a href="/wiki/Electric_generator" title="Electric generator">electric generators</a> which produce the electricity. Electricity can also be supplied by chemical sources such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_batteries" title="Electric batteries">electric batteries</a> or by other means from a wide variety of sources of energy. Electric power is generally supplied to businesses and homes by the <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_industry" title="Electric power industry">electric power industry</a>. Electricity is usually sold by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt_hour" title="Kilowatt hour">kilowatt hour</a> (3.6 MJ) which is the product of power in kilowatts multiplied by running time in hours. Electric utilities measure power using <a href="/wiki/Electricity_meter" title="Electricity meter">electricity meters</a>, which keep a running total of the electric energy delivered to a customer. Unlike fossil fuels, electricity is a low <a href="/wiki/Entropy" title="Entropy">entropy</a> form of energy and can be converted into motion or many other forms of energy with high efficiency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronics">Electronics</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arduino_ftdi_chip-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Arduino_ftdi_chip-1.jpg/220px-Arduino_ftdi_chip-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Arduino_ftdi_chip-1.jpg/330px-Arduino_ftdi_chip-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Arduino_ftdi_chip-1.jpg/440px-Arduino_ftdi_chip-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arduino_ftdi_chip-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Surface-mount_technology" title="Surface-mount technology">Surface mount</a> electronic components</div></div></div>
<p>Electronics deals with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_circuit" title="Electrical circuit">electrical circuits</a> that involve <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Active_component" title="Active component">active electrical components</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_tube" title="Vacuum tube">vacuum tubes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">transistors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diode" title="Diode">diodes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Optoelectronics" title="Optoelectronics">optoelectronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sensor" title="Sensor">sensors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">integrated circuits</a>, and associated passive interconnection technologies. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nonlinear" title="Nonlinear">nonlinear</a> behaviour of active components and their ability to control electron flows makes amplification of weak signals possible and electronics is widely used in <a href="/wiki/Information_processing" title="Information processing">information processing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Signal_processing" title="Signal processing">signal processing</a>. The ability of electronic devices to act as <a href="/wiki/Switch" title="Switch">switches</a> makes digital information processing possible. Interconnection technologies such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Circuit_board" title="Circuit board">circuit boards</a>, electronics packaging technology, and other varied forms of communication infrastructure complete circuit functionality and transform the mixed components into a regular working <a href="/wiki/System" title="System">system</a>.
</p><p>Today, most electronic devices use <a href="/wiki/Semiconductor" title="Semiconductor">semiconductor</a> components to perform electron control. The study of semiconductor devices and related technology is considered a branch of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solid_state_physics" title="Solid state physics">solid state physics</a>, whereas the design and construction of <a href="/wiki/Electronic_circuit" title="Electronic circuit">electronic circuits</a> to solve practical problems come under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronics_engineering" title="Electronics engineering">electronics engineering</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electromagnetic_wave">Electromagnetic wave</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_wave" title="Electromagnetic wave">Electromagnetic wave</a></div>
<p>Faraday's and Ampère's work showed that a time-varying magnetic field acted as a source of an electric field, and a time-varying electric field was a source of a magnetic field. Thus, when either field is changing in time, then a field of the other is necessarily induced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uniphysics_22-8"><a href="#cite_note-uniphysics-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 696–700">: 696–700 </span></sup> Such a phenomenon has the properties of a <a href="/wiki/Wave" title="Wave">wave</a>, and is naturally referred to as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_wave" title="Electromagnetic wave">electromagnetic wave</a>. Electromagnetic waves were analysed theoretically by <a href="/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell" title="James Clerk Maxwell">James Clerk Maxwell</a> in 1864. Maxwell developed a set of equations that could unambiguously describe the interrelationship between electric field, magnetic field, electric charge, and electric current. He could moreover prove that such a wave would necessarily travel at the <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">speed of light</a>, and thus light itself was a form of electromagnetic radiation. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maxwell%27s_Laws" title="Maxwell's Laws">Maxwell's Laws</a>, which unify light, fields, and charge are one of the great milestones of theoretical physics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uniphysics_22-9"><a href="#cite_note-uniphysics-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 696–700">: 696–700 </span></sup>
</p><p>Thus, the work of many researchers enabled the use of electronics to convert signals into <a href="/wiki/Radio_frequency" title="Radio frequency">high frequency</a> oscillating currents, and via suitably shaped conductors, electricity permits the transmission and reception of these signals via radio waves over very long distances.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production_and_uses">Production and uses</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Generation_and_transmission">Generation and transmission</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">Electricity generation</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">Electric power transmission</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mains_electricity" title="Mains electricity">Mains electricity</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gorskii_04414u.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3010" data-file-width="3329" decoding="async" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gorskii_04414u.jpg/300px-Gorskii_04414u.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gorskii_04414u.jpg/450px-Gorskii_04414u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gorskii_04414u.jpg/600px-Gorskii_04414u.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gorskii_04414u.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Early 20th-century <a href="/wiki/Alternator" title="Alternator">alternator</a> made in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, in the power generating hall of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydroelectric" title="Hydroelectric">hydroelectric</a> station (photograph by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prokudin-Gorsky" title="Prokudin-Gorsky">Prokudin-Gorsky</a>, 1905–1915).</div></div></div>
<p>In the 6th century BC, the Greek philosopher <a href="/wiki/Thales_of_Miletus" title="Thales of Miletus">Thales of Miletus</a> experimented with amber rods and these experiments were the first studies into the production of electrical energy. While this method, now known as the <a href="/wiki/Triboelectric_effect" title="Triboelectric effect">triboelectric effect</a>, can lift light objects and generate sparks, it is extremely inefficient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-batteries_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-batteries-67">[67]</a></sup> It was not until the invention of the <a href="/wiki/Voltaic_pile" title="Voltaic pile">voltaic pile</a> in the eighteenth century that a viable source of electricity became available. The voltaic pile, and its modern descendant, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">electrical battery</a>, store energy chemically and make it available on demand in the form of electrical energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-batteries_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-batteries-67">[67]</a></sup> The battery is a versatile and very common power source which is ideally suited to many applications, but its energy storage is finite, and once discharged it must be disposed of or recharged. For large electrical demands electrical energy must be generated and transmitted continuously over conductive transmission lines.
</p><p>Electrical power is usually generated by electro-mechanical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_generator" title="Electrical generator">generators</a> driven by <a href="/wiki/Steam" title="Steam">steam</a> produced from <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a> combustion, or the heat released from nuclear reactions; or from other sources such as <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a> extracted from wind or flowing water. The modern <a href="/wiki/Steam_turbine" title="Steam turbine">steam turbine</a> invented by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Algernon_Parsons" title="Charles Algernon Parsons">Sir Charles Parsons</a> in 1884 today generates about 80 percent of the <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">electric power</a> in the world using a variety of heat sources. Such generators bear no resemblance to Faraday's homopolar disc generator of 1831, but they still rely on his electromagnetic principle that a conductor linking a changing magnetic field induces a potential difference across its ends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The invention in the late nineteenth century of the <a href="/wiki/Transformer" title="Transformer">transformer</a> meant that electrical power could be transmitted more efficiently at a higher voltage but lower current. Efficient <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_transmission" title="Electrical transmission">electrical transmission</a> meant in turn that electricity could be generated at centralised <a href="/wiki/Power_station" title="Power station">power stations</a>, where it benefited from <a href="/wiki/Economies_of_scale" title="Economies of scale">economies of scale</a>, and then be despatched relatively long distances to where it was needed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Patterson_p44-48_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Patterson_p44-48-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parque_e%C3%B3lico_La_Muela.jpg"><img alt="A wind farm of about a dozen three-bladed white wind turbines." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Parque_e%C3%B3lico_La_Muela.jpg/220px-Parque_e%C3%B3lico_La_Muela.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Parque_e%C3%B3lico_La_Muela.jpg/330px-Parque_e%C3%B3lico_La_Muela.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Parque_e%C3%B3lico_La_Muela.jpg/440px-Parque_e%C3%B3lico_La_Muela.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parque_e%C3%B3lico_La_Muela.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">Wind power</a> is of increasing importance in many countries</div></div></div>
<p>Since electrical energy cannot easily be stored in quantities large enough to meet demands on a national scale, at all times exactly as much must be produced as is required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Patterson_p44-48_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Patterson_p44-48-69">[69]</a></sup> This requires <a href="/wiki/Electric_utility" title="Electric utility">electricity utilities</a> to make careful predictions of their electrical loads, and maintain constant co-ordination with their power stations. A certain amount of generation must always be held in <a href="/wiki/Operating_reserve" title="Operating reserve">reserve</a> to cushion an electrical grid against inevitable disturbances and losses.
</p><p>Demand for electricity grows with great rapidity as a nation modernises and its economy develops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The United States showed a 12% increase in demand during each year of the first three decades of the twentieth century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> a rate of growth that is now being experienced by emerging economies such as those of India or China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Historically, the growth rate for electricity demand has outstripped that for other forms of energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRC1986_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-NRC1986-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 16">: 16 </span></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_concerns_with_electricity_generation" title="Environmental concerns with electricity generation">Environmental concerns with electricity generation</a> have led to an increased focus on generation from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable sources</a>, in particular from <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind</a> and <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar</a>. While debate can be expected to continue over the environmental impact of different means of electricity production, its final form is relatively clean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRC1986_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-NRC1986-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 89">: 89 </span></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gluehlampe_01_KMJ.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1276" data-file-width="768" decoding="async" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gluehlampe_01_KMJ.png/170px-Gluehlampe_01_KMJ.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gluehlampe_01_KMJ.png/255px-Gluehlampe_01_KMJ.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gluehlampe_01_KMJ.png/340px-Gluehlampe_01_KMJ.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gluehlampe_01_KMJ.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Incandescent_light_bulb" title="Incandescent light bulb">light bulb</a>, an early application of electricity, operates by <a href="/wiki/Joule_heating" title="Joule heating">Joule heating</a>: the passage of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Current_(electricity)" title="Current (electricity)">current</a> through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_resistance" title="Electrical resistance">resistance</a> generating heat</div></div></div>
<p>Electricity is a very convenient way to transfer energy, and it has been adapted to a huge, and growing, number of uses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The invention of a practical <a href="/wiki/Incandescent_light_bulb" title="Incandescent light bulb">incandescent light bulb</a> in the 1870s led to <a href="/wiki/Lighting" title="Lighting">lighting</a> becoming one of the first publicly available applications of electrical power. Although electrification brought with it its own dangers, replacing the naked flames of gas lighting greatly reduced fire hazards within homes and factories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Public utilities were set up in many cities targeting the burgeoning market for electrical lighting. In the late 20th century and in modern times, the trend has started to flow in the direction of deregulation in the electrical power sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>The resistive <a href="/wiki/Joule_heating" title="Joule heating">Joule heating</a> effect employed in filament light bulbs also sees more direct use in <a href="/wiki/Electric_heating" title="Electric heating">electric heating</a>. While this is versatile and controllable, it can be seen as wasteful, since most electrical generation has already required the production of heat at a power station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> A number of countries, such as Denmark, have issued legislation restricting or banning the use of resistive electric heating in new buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Electricity is however still a highly practical energy source for heating and <a href="/wiki/Refrigeration" title="Refrigeration">refrigeration</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Air_conditioning" title="Air conditioning">air conditioning</a>/<a href="/wiki/Heat_pump" title="Heat pump">heat pumps</a> representing a growing sector for electricity demand for heating and cooling, the effects of which electricity utilities are increasingly obliged to accommodate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>Electricity is used within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">telecommunications</a>, and indeed the <a href="/wiki/Electrical_telegraph" title="Electrical telegraph">electrical telegraph</a>, demonstrated commercially in 1837 by <a href="/wiki/William_Fothergill_Cooke" title="William Fothergill Cooke">Cooke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Wheatstone" title="Charles Wheatstone">Wheatstone</a>, was one of its earliest applications. With the construction of first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Transcontinental_Telegraph" title="First Transcontinental Telegraph">transcontinental</a>, and then <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_telegraph_cable" title="Transatlantic telegraph cable">transatlantic</a>, telegraph systems in the 1860s, electricity had enabled communications in minutes across the globe. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Optical_fibre" title="Optical fibre">Optical fibre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communications_satellite" title="Communications satellite">satellite communication</a> have taken a share of the market for communications systems, but electricity can be expected to remain an essential part of the process.
</p><p>The effects of electromagnetism are most visibly employed in the <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motor</a>, which provides a clean and efficient means of motive power. A stationary motor such as a <a href="/wiki/Winch" title="Winch">winch</a> is easily provided with a supply of power, but a motor that moves with its application, such as an <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicle</a>, is obliged to either carry along a power source such as a battery, or to collect current from a sliding contact such as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pantograph_(rail)" title="Pantograph (rail)">pantograph</a>. Electrically powered vehicles are used in public transportation, such as electric buses and trains,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and an increasing number of battery-powered <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric cars</a> in private ownership.
</p><p>Electronic devices make use of the <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">transistor</a>, perhaps one of the most important inventions of the twentieth century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and a fundamental building block of all modern circuitry. A modern <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">integrated circuit</a> may contain many billions of miniaturised transistors in a region only a few centimetres square.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity_and_the_natural_world">Electricity and the natural world</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physiological_effects">Physiological effects</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_shock" title="Electric shock">Electric shock</a></div>
<p>A voltage applied to a human body causes an electric current through the tissues, and although the relationship is non-linear, the greater the voltage, the greater the current.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tleis_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-tleis-86">[86]</a></sup> The threshold for perception varies with the supply frequency and with the path of the current, but is about 0.1 mA to 1 mA for mains-frequency electricity, though a current as low as a microamp can be detected as an <a href="/wiki/Electrovibration" title="Electrovibration">electrovibration</a> effect under certain conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> If the current is sufficiently high, it will cause muscle contraction, <a href="/wiki/Fibrillation" title="Fibrillation">fibrillation</a> of the heart, and <a href="/wiki/Burn" title="Burn">tissue burns</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tleis_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-tleis-86">[86]</a></sup> The lack of any visible sign that a conductor is electrified makes electricity a particular hazard. The pain caused by an electric shock can be intense, leading electricity at times to be employed as a method of <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a>. Death caused by an electric shock is referred to as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_shock" title="Electric shock">electrocution</a>. Electrocution is still the means of <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">judicial execution</a> in some jurisdictions, though its use has become rarer in recent times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electrical_phenomena_in_nature">Electrical phenomena in nature</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electrical_phenomena" title="Electrical phenomena">Electrical phenomena</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Electric-eel2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Electric-eel2.jpg/220px-Electric-eel2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Electric-eel2.jpg/330px-Electric-eel2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Electric-eel2.jpg/440px-Electric-eel2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Electric-eel2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Electric_eel" title="Electric eel">electric eel</a>, <i>Electrophorus electricus</i></div></div></div>
<p>Electricity is not a human invention, and may be observed in several forms in nature, a prominent manifestation of which is <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a>. Many interactions familiar at the macroscopic level, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Touch" title="Touch">touch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friction" title="Friction">friction</a> or <a href="/wiki/Chemical_bond" title="Chemical bond">chemical bonding</a>, are due to interactions between electric fields on the atomic scale. The <a href="/wiki/Earth%27s_magnetic_field" title="Earth's magnetic field">Earth's magnetic field</a> is thought to arise from a <a href="/wiki/Dynamo_theory" title="Dynamo theory">natural dynamo</a> of circulating currents in the planet's core.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Certain crystals, such as <a href="/wiki/Quartz" title="Quartz">quartz</a>, or even <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>, generate a potential difference across their faces when subjected to external pressure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crystallography_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-crystallography-90">[90]</a></sup> This phenomenon is known as <a href="/wiki/Piezoelectricity" title="Piezoelectricity">piezoelectricity</a>, from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <i>piezein</i> (πιέζειν), meaning to press, and was discovered in 1880 by <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Curie" title="Pierre Curie">Pierre</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacques_Curie" title="Jacques Curie">Jacques Curie</a>. The effect is reciprocal, and when a piezoelectric material is subjected to an electric field, a small change in physical dimensions takes place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crystallography_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-crystallography-90">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bioelectrogenesis#Bioelectrogenesis_in_microbial_life" title="Bioelectrogenesis">§Bioelectrogenesis in microbial life</a> is a prominent phenomenon in soils and sediment ecology resulting from <a href="/wiki/Anaerobic_respiration" title="Anaerobic respiration">anaerobic respiration</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Microbial_fuel_cell" title="Microbial fuel cell">microbial fuel cell</a> mimics this ubiquitous natural phenomenon.
</p><p>Some organisms, such as <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">sharks</a>, are able to detect and respond to changes in electric fields, an ability known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electroreception" title="Electroreception">electroreception</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biodynamics_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Biodynamics-91">[91]</a></sup> while others, termed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrogenic" title="Electrogenic">electrogenic</a>, are able to generate voltages themselves to serve as a predatory or defensive weapon; these are <a href="/wiki/Electric_fish" title="Electric fish">electric fish</a> in different orders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Electroreception_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Electroreception-3">[3]</a></sup> The order <a href="/wiki/Gymnotiformes" title="Gymnotiformes">Gymnotiformes</a>, of which the best known example is the <a href="/wiki/Electric_eel" title="Electric eel">electric eel</a>, detect or stun their prey via high voltages generated from modified muscle cells called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrocytes" title="Electrocytes">electrocytes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Electroreception_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Electroreception-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morris_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-morris-4">[4]</a></sup> All animals transmit information along their cell membranes with voltage pulses called <a href="/wiki/Action_potential" title="Action potential">action potentials</a>, whose functions include communication by the nervous system between <a href="/wiki/Neuron" title="Neuron">neurons</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">muscles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neural_science_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-neural_science-92">[92]</a></sup> An electric shock stimulates this system, and causes muscles to contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Action potentials are also responsible for coordinating activities in certain plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neural_science_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-neural_science-92">[92]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_perception">Cultural perception</span></h2>
<p>In 1850, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Gladstone" title="William Gladstone">William Gladstone</a> asked the scientist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Faraday" title="Michael Faraday">Michael Faraday</a> why electricity was valuable. Faraday answered, “One day sir, you may tax it.”<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Conversation_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Conversation-94">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 19th and early 20th century, electricity was not part of the everyday life of many people, even in the industrialised <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">popular culture</a> of the time accordingly often depicted it as a mysterious, quasi-magical force that can slay the living, revive the dead or otherwise bend the laws of nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Riper_69_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Riper_69-95">[95]</a></sup> This attitude began with the 1771 experiments of <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Galvani" title="Luigi Galvani">Luigi Galvani</a> in which the legs of dead frogs were shown to twitch on application of <a href="/wiki/Galvanism" title="Galvanism">animal electricity</a>. "Revitalization" or resuscitation of apparently dead or drowned persons was reported in the medical literature shortly after Galvani's work. These results were known to <a href="/wiki/Mary_Shelley" title="Mary Shelley">Mary Shelley</a> when she authored <i><a href="/wiki/Frankenstein" title="Frankenstein">Frankenstein</a></i> (1819), although she does not name the method of revitalization of the monster. The revitalization of monsters with electricity later became a stock theme in horror films.
</p><p>As the public familiarity with electricity as the lifeblood of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Industrial_Revolution" title="Second Industrial Revolution">Second Industrial Revolution</a> grew, its wielders were more often cast in a positive light,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Riper_71_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Riper_71-96">[96]</a></sup> such as the workers who "finger death at their gloves' end as they piece and repiece the living wires" in <a href="/wiki/Rudyard_Kipling" title="Rudyard Kipling">Rudyard Kipling</a>'s 1907 poem <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sons_of_Martha" title="Sons of Martha">Sons of Martha</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Riper_71_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Riper_71-96">[96]</a></sup> Electrically powered vehicles of every sort featured large in adventure stories such as those of <a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne" title="Jules Verne">Jules Verne</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Tom_Swift" title="Tom Swift">Tom Swift</a></i> books.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Riper_71_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Riper_71-96">[96]</a></sup> The masters of electricity, whether fictional or real—including scientists such as <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Thomas Edison</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Steinmetz" title="Charles Steinmetz">Charles Steinmetz</a> or <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Tesla" title="Nikola Tesla">Nikola Tesla</a>—were popularly conceived of as having wizard-like powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Riper_71_96-3"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Riper_71-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>With electricity ceasing to be a novelty and becoming a necessity of everyday life in the later half of the 20th century, it required particular attention by popular culture only when it <i>stops</i> flowing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Riper_71_96-4"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Riper_71-96">[96]</a></sup> an event that usually signals disaster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Riper_71_96-5"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Riper_71-96">[96]</a></sup> The people who <i>keep</i> it flowing, such as the nameless hero of <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Webb" title="Jimmy Webb">Jimmy Webb</a>’s song "<a href="/wiki/Wichita_Lineman" title="Wichita Lineman">Wichita Lineman</a>" (1968),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Riper_71_96-6"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Riper_71-96">[96]</a></sup> are still often cast as heroic, wizard-like figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Riper_71_96-7"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Riper_71-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-55">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Almost all electric fields vary in space. An exception is the electric field surrounding a planar conductor of infinite extent, the field of which is uniform.</span>
